  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_17901eff-5115-49c6-bbc6-c18bda6950d3'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer369896652887635">It is autumn, 1941, and a German U-boat commander and his crew set out on yet another hazardous patrol in the Battle of the Atlantic. Over the coming weeks they must brave the stormy waters of the Atlantic in their mission to seek out and destroy British supply ships. But the tide is beginning to turn against the Germans in the war for the North Atlantic. Their targets now</span>
  <span id="freeText369896652887635" style="display:none">It is autumn, 1941, and a German U-boat commander and his crew set out on yet another hazardous patrol in the Battle of the Atlantic. Over the coming weeks they must brave the stormy waters of the Atlantic in their mission to seek out and destroy British supply ships. But the tide is beginning to turn against the Germans in the war for the North Atlantic. Their targets now travel in convoys, fiercely guarded by Royal Navy destroyers, and when contact is finally made the hunters rapidly become the hunted. As the U-boat is forced to hide beneath the surface of the sea a cat-and-mouse game begins, where the increasing claustrophobia of the submarine becomes an enemy just as frightening as the depth charges that explode around it. Of the 40,000 men who served on German submarines, 30,000 never returned. Written by a survivor of the U-boat fleet, <i>Das Boot </i>is a psychological drama merciless in its intensity, and a classic novel of World War II.</span>
  <a data-text-id="369896652887635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_61906379" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61906379" />
    <a title="Eric_W" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1711431-eric-w"><img alt="Eric_W" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550592937p2/1711431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61906379?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric_W" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric_W" href="/user/show/1711431-eric-w">Eric_W</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1711431-eric-w?shelf=nautical-fiction">nautical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1711431-eric-w?shelf=ww-ii">ww-ii</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61906379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3737206814661845177">Probably the most existential and realistic book of submarine warfare from the point of view of a German crew that I have read. It reveals an experience most would rather not have had to live through.<br/><br/>Submarines need buoyancy to function. Salt water makes that extremely difficult because the specific gravity of salt water varies with depth, temperature, the amount of plankton, salinity, even the time of year. (Apparently fresh water is much easier.) Now letâs assume that the specific gravity chan</span>
  <span id="freeText3737206814661845177" style="display:none">Probably the most existential and realistic book of submarine warfare from the point of view of a German crew that I have read. It reveals an experience most would rather not have had to live through.<br /><br />Submarines need buoyancy to function. Salt water makes that extremely difficult because the specific gravity of salt water varies with depth, temperature, the amount of plankton, salinity, even the time of year. (Apparently fresh water is much easier.) Now letâs assume that the specific gravity changes by 1/1000, a small enough amount. If the weight of the sub is 800 tons, the weight must change by 1/1000 or 1600 lbs., not an insignificant amount. The weight has to be increased or decreased as the case may be.<br /><br />Or letâs say the cook moves a 100 lb. sack of potatoes from the stern forward. That amount of weight has to be redistributed by pumping an equivalent amount of water back to the stern in the trim tanks. You will never think of submarines in quite the same way after you have read the description of their sub in the midst of a storm having to run on the surface for speed (if you could call it that) and to charge the batteries, the boat plunging and heaving through the waves. Can submarines capsize?<br /><br />This kind of fascinating information adds such verisimilitude to one of the submarine classics to come out of WW II. The author served as a naval correspondent on U-Boots during the war and experienced much of what he then wrote about. I have seen the movie (in German) and listened to the audiobook in addition to reading the book (in English). Not recommended in any form if you have a heart condition. <br /><br />âAll doubts are silenced by the concept of duty.â Think about that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3737206814661845177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1065088167974504615">Excellent true account of a young German sailor's time serving on a submarine during WWII.<br/>I can't praise this book enough. This was made into a miniseries which was one of the most hypnotic and thrilling I've ever seen. There was one lighthearted scene where the young sailors lustily sing their favorite song "It's a Long Way to Tipperary" that I found hilarious.</span>

<div id="review_190914578" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190914578" />
    <a title="El" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83144-el"><img alt="El" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479156984p2/83144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190914578?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="El" class="user" itemprop="url" name="El" href="/user/show/83144-el">El</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=20th-centurylit-late">20th-centurylit-late</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190914578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7235542767405491903">I don't remember how old I was when I saw this movie on TV, but I do recall how I felt. It terrified the piss out of me. But I couldn't look away. I'm not even sure if I saw the whole movie from beginning to end or if the bits I watched just made such an impression on me it feels now in retrospect like I watched it for hours, though I know in reality it couldn't possibly have been that way because of the circumstances surrounding how and when I saw it. It doesn't really matter. I don't ever want</span>
  <span id="freeText7235542767405491903" style="display:none">I don't remember how old I was when I saw this movie on TV, but I do recall how I felt. It terrified the piss out of me. But I couldn't look away. I'm not even sure if I saw the whole movie from beginning to end or if the bits I watched just made such an impression on me it feels now in retrospect like I watched it for hours, though I know in reality it couldn't possibly have been that way because of the circumstances surrounding how and when I saw it. It doesn't really matter. I don't ever want to be inside a submarine under water, thanks. I have enough trouble being inside a submarine above the water in the safety of a museum. <i>What if the door doesn't open?</i> No, thanks.<br /><br />Because of that viewing experience at what was obviously a very impressionable age, I've been curious to see the movie again (which will require some liquor to give me nerve) or to at least read the book. Books are safe, right? If my own imagination gets too intense I can just imagine a fluffy little puppy dog and a rainbow and everything is okay again.<br /><br />Except I realized as I was reading the book that I didn't want there to be a fluffy little puppy dog or a rainbow. I was totally invested in the story and I didn't want to even put it down. My eyes hurt if I read too long that I began to wonder if I was even blinking. It reads quickly, probably because it's hard not to keep turning the pages to see what happens next. I'm not normally that insane about reading, but I was excited by this story. I cared, dammit, this Buccheim guy totally made me care.<br /><br />I cared about all the sailor talk about whores and penises (penii?) and all the technical jargon that didn't make an iota of sense to me but omg it didn't even matter because it was interesting.<br /><br />Now I might be ready to watch the movie again. From what I remember the movie stayed pretty true to the novel, but the book loses out on all the German hotness because no one even speaks German really, outside of a few occasions. I seem to remember a lot of really wet, good-looking Germans in the movie. (Ah, so obviously I was old enough to have some sort of sexual attraction when I saw the film, or at least old enough to have imagined they were really hot German guys because looking at <a href="http://www.imdb.com/video/screenplay/vi2055707673/" rel="nofollow noopener">the trailer</a> now I don't see any particularly hot German guys - though Jurgen Prochnow isn't really much to sneeze at. Note: Watching that trailer just made me have heart palpitations. And now I have to go for a really long walk to get over this feeling that something large is sitting on my chest again.)<br /><br />The cover of my copy claims Das Boot is "One of the best novels ever written about war". If someone knows of a better one, please let me know. I will totally read it and let you know if I agree. Maybe I haven't read enough war novels but I was plenty impressed by this one.<br /><br /><br />Note: For extra special effect, I recommend reading this book on either a speeding bus driven by a maniacal Port Authority driver on a route that involves a lot of potholes and curves; make sure to be stuck between a window and a really fat, smelly man so you get the impression of being stuck. That was one of my experiences while reading the book and it really made me feel like I was on a submarine. The only thing really missing was the water and the (possibly) hot German guys.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7235542767405491903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1201055477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12406816935111849123">This book is about 550 pages long, and for the first 300 pages I was wondering what it was all about and why I was wasting my time. A hundred pages just described the sea. Another hundred pages gave details of the submarine. The third hundred pages described a never-ending storm (spoiler: it does end). <br/><br/>After that, though, the book is great. The tension is incredible. I felt actually sorry for the characters, and glad that I wasn't them. The ending was fittingly unhappy for a war book - I felt no</span>
  <span id="freeText12406816935111849123" style="display:none">This book is about 550 pages long, and for the first 300 pages I was wondering what it was all about and why I was wasting my time. A hundred pages just described the sea. Another hundred pages gave details of the submarine. The third hundred pages described a never-ending storm (spoiler: it does end). <br /><br />After that, though, the book is great. The tension is incredible. I felt actually sorry for the characters, and glad that I wasn't them. The ending was fittingly unhappy for a war book - I felt no joy or relief, only a general sense of "what a fucked up situation." Perhaps the book could have left the first 300 pages out, or perhaps the last half was only so good because of the incredibly long build up.</span>

<div id="review_2982408414" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2982408414" />
    <a title="Marquise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4674014-marquise"><img alt="Marquise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445405166p2/4674014.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_254010936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/254010936" />
    <a title="Corto" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5914786-corto"><img alt="Corto" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312570307p2/5914786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/254010936?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corto" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corto" href="/user/show/5914786-corto">Corto</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254010936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9386612683647011263">I have a hard time reading novels from the German perspective on WWII. They usually all contain the same type of apologist rhetoric ("Nazi's suck! We're just fighting for the Fatherland, We don't really hate the Jews, Why I have a Jewish friend/I slept with a Jewish girl once blah-blah-blah", etc.). It's generally expressed in the first few pages so the reader knows that *these boys* are ok. It's grating every time I read it. Das Boot is no different. Having said that, this was a good, intense a</span>
  <span id="freeText9386612683647011263" style="display:none">I have a hard time reading novels from the German perspective on WWII. They usually all contain the same type of apologist rhetoric ("Nazi's suck! We're just fighting for the Fatherland, We don't really hate the Jews, Why I have a Jewish friend/I slept with a Jewish girl once blah-blah-blah", etc.). It's generally expressed in the first few pages so the reader knows that *these boys* are ok. It's grating every time I read it. Das Boot is no different. Having said that, this was a good, intense and gritty sea story. It humanized ze Germans and it was full of sturm and drang. However, I was never really able to weep for the boys on the boat throughout their trials and tribulations. Worth a read though if you're in the mood for something WWII-y and North Atlantic-y.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9386612683647011263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2194365511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194365511" />
    <a title="Paul Ataua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33831018-paul-ataua"><img alt="Paul Ataua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407668489p2/33831018.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2194365511?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Ataua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Ataua" href="/user/show/33831018-paul-ataua">Paul Ataua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2194365511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer854454114987290461">Submarine war novels are not usually my kind of thing and this one was possibly a couple of hundred pages too long, but âDas Bootâ was worth reading. It is always so easy to understand the horror of war on an intellectual level, but âDas Bootâ takes you further and engages you in the terror of war. You actually get to feel the claustrophobia, the desperation, and the feeling of helplessness under fire. I never watched the movie, but may do now.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_391630925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/391630925?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Foshee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Foshee" href="/user/show/5084771-scott-foshee">Scott Foshee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer391630925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11420512834936455452">This important book is not about nations or ideologies. It is not about what side was right or wrong in WWII. It is about regular men in the throes of war, fighting for their families, their comrades, and for their very lives. Das Boot does not glorify war. On the contrary, it highlights the fact that we are all human and are all basically the same on the level of the individual. It illustrates that one of the horrors of war rarely mentioned is that the outcome is often decided by brute force, r</span>
  <span id="freeText11420512834936455452" style="display:none">This important book is not about nations or ideologies. It is not about what side was right or wrong in WWII. It is about regular men in the throes of war, fighting for their families, their comrades, and for their very lives. Das Boot does not glorify war. On the contrary, it highlights the fact that we are all human and are all basically the same on the level of the individual. It illustrates that one of the horrors of war rarely mentioned is that the outcome is often decided by brute force, regardless of right, wrong, or ideology. The individual is caught in the middle, merely doing his best for what he believes is right.<br /><br />Das Boot follows one German submarine on one patrol in the north Atlantic during WWII when the war is beginning to turn. We live in close quarters for weeks with the fictional crew of U-96, a Type VIIC-class U-boat. We feel the stifling claustrophobia of a WWII era submarine, the boredom of fruitless searches for the enemy, the tedium and fright of a month-long Atlantic hurricane, the thrill of the hunt, and the abject terror of the hunter becoming the hunted.<br /><br />The intensity of Das Boot is something I have rarely experienced in a book. I found myself reading late into the night, huddled with the silent crew at impossible depths, listening to the creaking, the dripping condensation and the popping rivets of U-96 while awaiting the next depth charge attack. You can feel the sweat, you can taste the salt, and you can feel the shattering explosions rocking the control room.<br /><br />75% of German submariners during WWII died on patrol, which makes Das Boot one of the very few surviving accounts of what that brutal life was like. Lothar-GÃ¼nther Buchheim spent time on German subs during the war as a correspondent, and this fictionalized testament is a very valuable document of life "on the other side." In the U.S. most WWII accounts paint German fighting men with a very broad brush. Buchheim takes on a very controversial and difficult task by humanizing them. There are no heroes or false bravado here. The crew has a Christmas tree on board. They talk about their families, their sweethearts and their childhoods. They get their hands dirty and yearn to see the sky once again.<br /><br />It may be true that victors write the histories, but it is important to remember that real people serve on both sides in any war. Highly recommended.<br /> <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="11420512834936455452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3811201284947928965">For some reason I've become fascinated with submarine warfare during WWII. The Smithsonian Chanel has been running a series call Hell Below. I've also recently read a few non-fiction of accounts of submarines in action. Of course, for me and many others the best film about subs is Das Boot. I've seen it several times and think it's one of the greatest war movies ever made. So I was curious to try the book, upon which the movie was made. The plot and characters are very similar and some of the ac</span>
  <span id="freeText3811201284947928965" style="display:none">For some reason I've become fascinated with submarine warfare during WWII. The Smithsonian Chanel has been running a series call Hell Below. I've also recently read a few non-fiction of accounts of submarines in action. Of course, for me and many others the best film about subs is Das Boot. I've seen it several times and think it's one of the greatest war movies ever made. So I was curious to try the book, upon which the movie was made. The plot and characters are very similar and some of the action. But what this book did for me was give me a real sense of what it was like to be so vulnerable. There are several scenes of depth charge attacks that gave me chills. There is one scene not in the film which had my heart beating faster. For some the myriad descriptions about how submarines work and information about currents and navigation may be a bit much. Though in the spirit of the story these things are worth knowing. In reality this fell just short of five stars but since there is no 4-and-half star review I gave it five.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3811201284947928965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14082200134858219617">I'm really torn on how to rate this. I knew it was a classic going in and decided it was about time I got around to it after reading Dead Wake by Erik Larson. I imagine that the purpose of the book was to show how awful the experience was the officers assigned to U-boats. The author did a fantastic job of giving a detailed blow-by-blow of daily life under a variety of circumstances from attack to counterattack, from calm seas to storms, from departure to arrival. Here was my problem: it was so i</span>
  <span id="freeText14082200134858219617" style="display:none">I'm really torn on how to rate this. I knew it was a classic going in and decided it was about time I got around to it after reading Dead Wake by Erik Larson. I imagine that the purpose of the book was to show how awful the experience was the officers assigned to U-boats. The author did a fantastic job of giving a detailed blow-by-blow of daily life under a variety of circumstances from attack to counterattack, from calm seas to storms, from departure to arrival. Here was my problem: it was so incredibly detailed that it became monotonous. Page after page talking about how they had to stay submerged because of a storm that lasted for weeks. The sheer length of each scene was torturous; I enjoy reading well-detailed and descriptive prose, but this was a whole new level. To the author's credit, it made me feel truly immersed in the unpleasantness of such a life. However, the scenes dragged on interminably to the point that it made me want to stop reading and give up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14082200134858219617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/828561947?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jesse Kraai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesse Kraai" href="/user/show/3110985-jesse-kraai">Jesse Kraai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3110985-jesse-kraai?shelf=the-best">the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3110985-jesse-kraai?shelf=german">german</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer828561947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12017211231732028249">Yes, I saw the movie first, many times. I craved the pinging echoes and the claustrophobia of men living like rats. No triumphant American army come to sweep up the European debris of 1944, flexing muscles that havenât know suffering.<br/>The film gives a sensual experience of war. The book gives us the rest. We begin with monotonous boredom, captured with endless descriptions of the different shades of gray and wet that the sea gives the few who are allowed onto the small deck. The reader also wants</span>
  <span id="freeText12017211231732028249" style="display:none">Yes, I saw the movie first, many times. I craved the pinging echoes and the claustrophobia of men living like rats. No triumphant American army come to sweep up the European debris of 1944, flexing muscles that havenât know suffering.<br />The film gives a sensual experience of war. The book gives us the rest. We begin with monotonous boredom, captured with endless descriptions of the different shades of gray and wet that the sea gives the few who are allowed onto the small deck. The reader also wants to blow some shit up, even if it is just mostly cargo.<br />We get German/Prussian chain of command. No American bullshit where we kinda obey because thatâs what we were taught to do in boot camp, with an angry man shouting at us. The souls of these motherfuckers obey.<br />The Boot is the protagonist of the book. The machine has to be trusted, loved, understood. Only it can bring us back home. The boat is also the only one without hatred, political difference and the stupidity of Europe to slaughter itself. The boat is pure. It is rational and beautiful.<br />Buchheimâs Boot is his post-war therapy. The story places him as part of the machine. He obeys as serenely as the many wonderful pistons and valves. He is as pure as the boat. And his painterâs eyes come up with hundreds of colorful memories to name the blues and grays of the ocean.<br />This will to delusion is Buchheimâs survival strategy. It gets him through the war and then negotiates his successful return to life in post-war Germany, where he quickly bought up artwork that the Nazis had devalued with the degenerate label. They were colorful paintings. On the left we have two of Ernst Kirchnerâs paintings. Dude shot himself in 38 after most of his work had been burned. Buchheim got a good price.<br />Buchheimâs book is what for me the novel is all about. He allows me into the interior world of the Nazi experience. <br /></span>

<div id="review_193340703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193340703" />
    <a title="Ian Kemp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5942350-ian-kemp"><img alt="Ian Kemp" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193340703?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian Kemp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian Kemp" href="/user/show/5942350-ian-kemp">Ian Kemp</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193340703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12028538902848703205">Buchheim has an illustrative style which in other writers can be very tiresome - but somehow in this book it serves to highlight the extreme psychological stress of life on a WW2 U-boat - the claustrophobia, helplessness under fire, the total reliance on the split-second judgements of one man, the 30 year old commander they call 'The Old Man'. The only recourse for an individual trapped in this hell is to withdraw into an internal reality in which past events, opportunities taken and opportuniti</span>
  <span id="freeText12028538902848703205" style="display:none">Buchheim has an illustrative style which in other writers can be very tiresome - but somehow in this book it serves to highlight the extreme psychological stress of life on a WW2 U-boat - the claustrophobia, helplessness under fire, the total reliance on the split-second judgements of one man, the 30 year old commander they call 'The Old Man'. The only recourse for an individual trapped in this hell is to withdraw into an internal reality in which past events, opportunities taken and opportunities missed are examined in the same minute detail as the internal features of the boat, and the colours and textures of the waves and the clouds on the rare excursions to the tower. The only thing which goes unexamined is the future: best not to think beyond the immediate, in a world where life can be snatched away in an instant. The real shock of this book is that it is first hand documentary written by one of the few that got away.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12028538902848703205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13647390373765512746" style="display:none">When reading this I kept wanting to compare it to Sharks and Little Fish (another âhistorical fictionâ piece on the U-boat campaign of WWII), both have their moments of shine and Iâm certain veterans of the campaign appreciate them more than we might.<br />There are many things to love in Das Boot; the description of the attacks, the total boredom of daily operations, to the anticipation of circumstances. All of these make for a good story that goes toward great! <br />But if this is the case why only 4 stars.... the simple answer become Mr. Buchheimâs descriptions are sometimes lacking, confusing (the first chapter), or incomplete. Honestly at times it made it a little difficult (I understand the German writers are often different than Americans with how they tell their story; Iâve read several different ones and have to say Mr. Buchheimâs sections where heâs âlackingâ are some of the worst of German writers that Iâve read to date). Because of this the book becomes a 4 star book and in the battle between Das Boot and Sharks and Little Fish, Das Boot finishes second. What I will add is that I admire Wolfgang Petersen and his adaptation of Das Boot to the big screen; excellent capture of a book!</span>

<div id="review_2759762885" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2759762885" />
    <a title="Tyler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5336457-tyler"><img alt="Tyler" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2759762885?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tyler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tyler" href="/user/show/5336457-tyler">Tyler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780394491059" href="/book/show/1353810.The_Boat">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5336457-tyler?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2759762885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12946334225895903733">I rounded up to 5 on this one. From the perspective of an on-board war correspondent, the novel follows one U-Boat tour in the Atlantic during the winter of 1940. The book is a mix sheer boredom and occasional helpless terror from British boats, weeks of storms, or the workings of The Boat itself.<br/><br/>The characters feel realistic. The manager of my friendly local Erbert & Gerbert's told me that this book was (is?) required reading at US Naval Academy. Wouldn't surprise me because of The Old Man, the</span>
  <span id="freeText12946334225895903733" style="display:none">I rounded up to 5 on this one. From the perspective of an on-board war correspondent, the novel follows one U-Boat tour in the Atlantic during the winter of 1940. The book is a mix sheer boredom and occasional helpless terror from British boats, weeks of storms, or the workings of The Boat itself.<br /><br />The characters feel realistic. The manager of my friendly local Erbert &amp; Gerbert's told me that this book was (is?) required reading at US Naval Academy. Wouldn't surprise me because of The Old Man, the boat's commander who at 30 years old is an old veteran at the U-Boat group. He's a great character, always cool and leading by example, and the narrator follows him closely. <br /><br />The narrator definitely isn't a Nazi and has some digs at a true believer, but in the end he is going with the flow. <br /><br />The book's intense, claustrophobic, surprisingly sexual (conversations/memories), and also very informational about U-Boats, their crews, and the Atlantic part of the war. The writer calls it "a novel but not fiction," as each of the events is something he experienced as a U-Boat war correspondent. <br /><br /><br />4.8/5 Definitely read if you want historical war fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12946334225895903733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Stephen mcneil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93700804-stephen-mcneil"><img alt="Stephen mcneil" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen mcneil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen mcneil" href="/user/show/93700804-stephen-mcneil">Stephen mcneil</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3445539500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16738915530930549302">So good! Written with the sincerity only an author who himself experienced the terror of underwater warfare could provide. To describe the book as thrilling would be an understatement - this book makes you sit up straight, delivering a 'straight to the gut' personification of the rigor, vulgarity, and grit required of U-boat crewmen. The author was a renowned collector of expressionist artists - it shows in his writing, a delightful mixture of poetry and prose which never becomes emotive or dist</span>
  <span id="freeText16738915530930549302" style="display:none">So good! Written with the sincerity only an author who himself experienced the terror of underwater warfare could provide. To describe the book as thrilling would be an understatement - this book makes you sit up straight, delivering a 'straight to the gut' personification of the rigor, vulgarity, and grit required of U-boat crewmen. The author was a renowned collector of expressionist artists - it shows in his writing, a delightful mixture of poetry and prose which never becomes emotive or distracting. The palatable strain is felt until the last page (reluctantly turned, no less). A keeper that will be read again and again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16738915530930549302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2217945133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <a title="Bob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bob" href="/user/show/9392539-bob">Bob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2217945133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10643472920370345779">This is an incredible book and very well written and easy to read. The movie version follows the book fairly closely although there is much more detail in the book. The incredible conditions that these German sailors faced is hard to believe. The stark changes from very boring to sailing through a two week storm and then experiencing intense and prolonged depth charge attacks is just incredible. The book also reminds me in some ways of All Quite on the Western Front. Although the nature of the e</span>
  <span id="freeText10643472920370345779" style="display:none">This is an incredible book and very well written and easy to read. The movie version follows the book fairly closely although there is much more detail in the book. The incredible conditions that these German sailors faced is hard to believe. The stark changes from very boring to sailing through a two week storm and then experiencing intense and prolonged depth charge attacks is just incredible. The book also reminds me in some ways of All Quite on the Western Front. Although the nature of the experience of a submariner compared to a WWI infantryman is quite different.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10643472920370345779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2608915907?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terry Cornell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terry Cornell" href="/user/show/11712998-terry-cornell">Terry Cornell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11712998-terry-cornell?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2608915907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10316050400061044683">Although this book is fiction, the author served in the German Navy during World War II on various ships including submarines. I read this many years ago when I was in high school, and at the time thought parts describing the functioning of the submarine tedious. Now, I find those parts much more interesting. The movie 'Das Boot' was based on this book. It seems like the crew of this sub goes through more horrors of war than most, however it does a great job of putting the reader in the experien</span>
  <span id="freeText10316050400061044683" style="display:none">Although this book is fiction, the author served in the German Navy during World War II on various ships including submarines. I read this many years ago when I was in high school, and at the time thought parts describing the functioning of the submarine tedious. Now, I find those parts much more interesting. The movie 'Das Boot' was based on this book. It seems like the crew of this sub goes through more horrors of war than most, however it does a great job of putting the reader in the experience. As I was reading the book this time round, I realized the dialogue seemed to have a British tone. I determined this is probably because the translator was British. Just as fascinating as the book, the bio of the author probably deserves it's own book. Mr. Bucheim was well known as a painter and artist as a teen, and worked as an illustrator for newspapers and magazines before the war. During the war, after serving on several ships, he eventually became a naval correspondent. After the war he opened a workshop for handicrafts and an art gallery. He collected an impressive collection of German Impressionist paintings. In addition to his novels on the German navy, Mr. Buchheim also wrote several books on Expressionism and monographs on several well known artists and started his own art publishing company.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10316050400061044683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It is written sensitively about the many very young men that went to sea and how arbitrary it became as to whether they survived or died. This was a very well regarded and successful movie and a book that I had hoped to read ever since it's publication. I was not dissappointed.</span>

<div id="review_2248670412" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2248670412" />

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2248670412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8347631536798919241">A novel with detail such as that written by Tom Clancy and Arthur Hailey, "Das Boot" immerses (pun intended) the reader in a WWII German U-boat. The boredom, the hunt, the terror, the punishment are all deeply (pun intended) felt by the reader. I thoroughly enjoyed Buchheim's story, and recommend it.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('W8dsxS5JVfIneK2lu6BgLykxeXWd5Rfty/vY5jBrl2fXhroNSPmnnSNYVT57uJbPmi/S+ZfCJ4/KElAF4EwxTA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
